<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Number in {..., –2, –1, 0, 1, 2, ...} </div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For computer representation, see <a href="/wiki/Integer_(computer_science)" title="Integer (computer science)">Integer (computer science)</a>. For the generalization in algebraic number theory, see <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_integer" title="Algebraic integer">Algebraic integer</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<div class="sidebar-list mw-collapsible mw-collapsed"><div class="sidebar-list-title" style="background:transparent;border-top:1px solid #aaa;text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Algebraic_group" title="Algebraic group">Algebraic groups</a></div><div class="sidebar-list-content mw-collapsible-content hlist" style="border-top:1px solid #aaa;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;">

</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Group_theory_sidebar" title="Template:Group theory sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Group_theory_sidebar" title="Template talk:Group theory sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Group_theory_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>An <b>integer</b> is the number zero (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/0_(number)" title="0 (number)">0</a>), a positive <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">natural number</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_(number)" title="1 (number)">1</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2_(number)" title="2 (number)">2</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3_(number)" title="3 (number)">3</a>, etc.) or a <b>negative integer</b> with a minus sign (<a href="/wiki/%E2%88%921" title="−1">−1</a>, −2, −3, etc.).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Negative_number" title="Negative number">negative numbers</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Additive_inverse" title="Additive inverse">additive inverses</a> of the corresponding positive numbers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Language_of_mathematics" title="Language of mathematics">language of mathematics</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Set_(mathematics)" title="Set (mathematics)">set</a> of integers is often denoted by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boldface" title="Boldface">boldface</a> <span class="texhtml"><b>Z</b></span> or <a href="/wiki/Blackboard_bold" title="Blackboard bold">blackboard bold</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earliest_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-earliest-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cameron1998_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cameron1998-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>The set of natural numbers <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {N} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">N</mi>
</mrow>

</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {N} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {N} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fdf9a96b565ea202d0f4322e9195613fb26a9bed" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is a <a href="/wiki/Subset" title="Subset">subset</a> of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, which in turn is a subset of the set of all <a href="/wiki/Rational_number" title="Rational number">rational numbers</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Q</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Q} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c5909f0b54e4718fa24d5fd34d54189d24a66e9a" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.808ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, itself a subset of the <a href="/wiki/Real_number" title="Real number">real numbers</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {R} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/786849c765da7a84dbc3cce43e96aad58a5868dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[a]</a></sup> Like the natural numbers, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is <a href="/wiki/Countable_set" title="Countable set">countably infinite</a>. An integer may be regarded as a real number that can be written without a <a href="/wiki/Fraction" title="Fraction">fractional component</a>. For example, 21, 4, 0, and −2048 are integers, while 9.75, <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1050945101">.mw-parser-output .sfrac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .sfrac.tion,.mw-parser-output .sfrac .tion{display:inline-block;vertical-align:-0.5em;font-size:85%;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .sfrac .num,.mw-parser-output .sfrac .den{display:block;line-height:1em;margin:0 0.1em}.mw-parser-output .sfrac .den{border-top:1px solid}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="sfrac" role="math">5<span class="sr-only">+</span><span class="tion"><span class="num">1</span><span class="sr-only">/</span><span class="den">2</span></span></span>, and <span class="texhtml"><span class="nowrap">√<span style="border-top:1px solid; padding:0 0.1em;">2</span></span></span> are not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>The integers form the smallest <a href="/wiki/Group_(mathematics)" title="Group (mathematics)">group</a> and the smallest <a href="/wiki/Ring_(mathematics)" title="Ring (mathematics)">ring</a> containing the <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">natural numbers</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_number_theory" title="Algebraic number theory">algebraic number theory</a>, the integers are sometimes qualified as <b>rational integers</b> to distinguish them from the more general <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_integer" title="Algebraic integer">algebraic integers</a>. In fact, (rational) integers are algebraic integers that are also <a href="/wiki/Rational_number" title="Rational number">rational numbers</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<p>The word integer comes from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/integer#Latin" title="wikt:integer"><i>integer</i></a> meaning "whole" or (literally) "untouched", from <i>in</i> ("not") plus <i>tangere</i> ("to touch"). "<a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/entire" title="wikt:entire">Entire</a>" derives from the same origin via the <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> word <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/entier" title="wikt:entier">entier</a></i>, which means both <i>entire</i> and <i>integer</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> Historically the term was used for a <a href="/wiki/Number" title="Number">number</a> that was a multiple of 1,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> or to the whole part of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed_number" title="Mixed number">mixed number</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> Only positive integers were considered, making the term synonymous with the <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">natural numbers</a>. The definition of integer expanded over time to include <a href="/wiki/Negative_number" title="Negative number">negative numbers</a> as their usefulness was recognized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-negmath_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-negmath-16">[15]</a></sup> For example <a href="/wiki/Leonhard_Euler" title="Leonhard Euler">Leonhard Euler</a> in his 1765 <a href="/wiki/Elements_of_Algebra" title="Elements of Algebra">Elements of Algebra</a> defined integers to include both positive and negative numbers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> However, European mathematicians, for the most part, resisted the concept of negative numbers until the middle of the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-negmath_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-negmath-16">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>The use of the letter Z to denote the set of integers comes from the <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> word <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Zahlen" title="wikt:Zahlen">Zahlen</a></i> ("number")<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earliest_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-earliest-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cameron1998_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cameron1998-5">[5]</a></sup> and has been attributed to <a href="/wiki/David_Hilbert" title="David Hilbert">David Hilbert</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> The earliest known use of the notation in a textbook occurs in <a href="/wiki/%C3%89l%C3%A9ments_de_math%C3%A9matique" title="Éléments de mathématique">Algébre</a> written by the collective <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Bourbaki" title="Nicolas Bourbaki">Nicolas Bourbaki</a>, dating to 1947.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earliest_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-earliest-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> The notation was not adopted immediately, for example another textbook used the letter J<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> and a 1960 paper used Z to denote the non-negative integers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> But by 1961, Z was generally used by modern algebra texts to denote the positive and negative integers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>The symbol <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is often annotated to denote various sets, with varying usage amongst different authors: <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} ^{+}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} ^{0+}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} ^{0+}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81a3b6ad192693a6aeb684d1876f82d852fcc228" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.883ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> or <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} ^{\geq }}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>≥<!-- ≥ --></mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} ^{\geq }}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} ^{\geq }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2d1683538868e87548cd2a6dd28c28dfab75ff44" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.061ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> for non-negative integers, and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} ^{\neq }}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>≠<!-- ≠ --></mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} ^{\neq }}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} ^{\neq }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0413be677c88a720f7f2d2593da069808bbc252a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.061ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> for non-zero integers. Some authors use <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} ^{*}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>∗<!-- ∗ --></mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} ^{*}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} ^{*}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/45aa6a166e406bf9e192b7a32d6b140f27cd8538" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.605ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> for non-zero integers, while others use it for non-negative integers, or for <span class="texhtml">{–1, 1}</span> (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Group_of_units" title="Group of units">group of units</a> of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>). Additionally, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} _{p}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>p</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} _{p}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} _{p}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dbc1df7227ef11fe88dccd2dae3adc7bbdeae5f4" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.609ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> is used to denote either the set of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Integers_modulo_n" title="Integers modulo n">integers modulo <span class="texhtml"><i>p</i></span></a> (i.e., the set of <a href="/wiki/Congruence_relation" title="Congruence relation">congruence classes</a> of integers), or the set of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P-adic_integer" title="P-adic integer"><span class="texhtml"><i>p</i></span>-adic integers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edexcelc1_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-edexcelc1-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>The whole numbers were synonymous with the integers up until the early 1950s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> In the late 1950s, as part of the <a href="/wiki/New_Math" title="New Math">New Math</a> movement,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> American elementary school teachers began teaching that "whole numbers" referred to the <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">natural numbers</a>, excluding negative numbers, while "integer" included the negative numbers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> "Whole number" remains ambiguous to the present day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Algebraic_properties">Algebraic properties</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Number-line.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="50" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Number-line.svg/300px-Number-line.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Number-line.svg/450px-Number-line.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Number-line.svg/600px-Number-line.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Number-line.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Integers can be thought of as discrete, equally spaced points on an infinitely long <a href="/wiki/Number_line" title="Number line">number line</a>. In the above, non-<a href="/wiki/Sign_(mathematics)#Terminology_for_signs" title="Sign (mathematics)">negative</a> integers are shown in blue and negative integers in red.</div></div></div>

<p><b><a href="/wiki/Algebraic_geometry" title="Algebraic geometry">Algebraic geometry</a></b>

</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-content">
<div class="sidebar-list mw-collapsible mw-collapsed"><div class="sidebar-list-title" style="text-align:center;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Noncommutative_algebra" title="Noncommutative algebra">Noncommutative algebra</a></div><div class="sidebar-list-content mw-collapsible-content" style="text-align: left;"><b><a href="/wiki/Noncommutative_ring" title="Noncommutative ring">Noncommutative rings</a></b>

<p><b><a href="/wiki/Noncommutative_algebraic_geometry" title="Noncommutative algebraic geometry">Noncommutative algebraic geometry</a></b>
</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Free_algebra" title="Free algebra">Free algebra</a></b>
</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Clifford_algebra" title="Clifford algebra">Clifford algebra</a></b>
</p>
<dl><dd>• <a href="/wiki/Geometric_algebra" title="Geometric algebra">Geometric algebra</a></dd></dl>
<b><a href="/wiki/Operator_algebra" title="Operator algebra">Operator algebra</a></b></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Ring_theory_sidebar" title="Template:Ring theory sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Ring_theory_sidebar" title="Template talk:Ring theory sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Ring_theory_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_numbers" title="Natural numbers">natural numbers</a>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is <a href="/wiki/Closure_(mathematics)" title="Closure (mathematics)">closed</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Binary_operation" title="Binary operation">operations</a> of addition and <a href="/wiki/Multiplication" title="Multiplication">multiplication</a>, that is, the sum and product of any two integers is an integer. However, with the inclusion of the negative natural numbers (and importantly, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/0_(number)" title="0 (number)">0</a>), <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, unlike the natural numbers, is also closed under <a href="/wiki/Subtraction" title="Subtraction">subtraction</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>The integers form a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unital_ring" title="Unital ring">unital ring</a> which is the most basic one, in the following sense: for any unital ring, there is a unique <a href="/wiki/Ring_homomorphism" title="Ring homomorphism">ring homomorphism</a> from the integers into this ring. This <a href="/wiki/Universal_property" title="Universal property">universal property</a>, namely to be an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Initial_object" title="Initial object">initial object</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Category_of_rings" title="Category of rings">category of rings</a>, characterizes the ring <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>.
</p><p><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is not closed under <a href="/wiki/Division_(mathematics)" title="Division (mathematics)">division</a>, since the quotient of two integers (e.g., 1 divided by 2) need not be an integer. Although the natural numbers are closed under <a href="/wiki/Exponentiation" title="Exponentiation">exponentiation</a>, the integers are not (since the result can be a fraction when the exponent is negative).
</p><p>The following table lists some of the basic properties of addition and multiplication for any integers <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i></span>, <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i></span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>c</i></span>:
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; border: none;">
<caption>Properties of addition and multiplication on integers
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>
</th>
<th scope="col">Addition
</th>
<th scope="col">Multiplication
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Closure_(mathematics)" title="Closure (mathematics)">Closure</a>:
</th>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> + <i>b</i></span><span style="padding-left:1em;"> </span>is an integer
</td>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> × <i>b</i></span><span style="padding-left:1em;"> </span>is an integer
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associativity" title="Associativity">Associativity</a>:
</th>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> + (<i>b</i> + <i>c</i>) = (<i>a</i> + <i>b</i>) + <i>c</i></span>
</td>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> × (<i>b</i> × <i>c</i>) = (<i>a</i> × <i>b</i>) × <i>c</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commutativity" title="Commutativity">Commutativity</a>:
</th>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> + <i>b</i> = <i>b</i> + <i>a</i></span>
</td>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> × <i>b</i> = <i>b</i> × <i>a</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Existence of an <a href="/wiki/Identity_element" title="Identity element">identity element</a>:
</th>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> + 0 = <i>a</i></span>
</td>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> × 1 = <i>a</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Existence of <a href="/wiki/Inverse_element" title="Inverse element">inverse elements</a>:
</th>
<td><span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> + (−<i>a</i>) = 0</span>
</td>
<td>The only invertible integers (called <a href="/wiki/Unit_(ring_theory)" title="Unit (ring theory)">units</a>) are <span class="texhtml">−1</span> and <span class="texhtml">1</span>.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distributivity" title="Distributivity">Distributivity</a>:
</th>
<td align="center" colspan="2"><span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> × (<i>b</i> + <i>c</i>) = (<i>a</i> × <i>b</i>) + (<i>a</i> × <i>c</i>)</span><span style="padding-left:1em;"> </span>and<span style="padding-left:1em;"> </span><span class="texhtml">(<i>a</i> + <i>b</i>) × <i>c</i> = (<i>a</i> × <i>c</i>) + (<i>b</i> × <i>c</i>)</span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">No <a href="/wiki/Zero_divisor" title="Zero divisor">zero divisors</a>:
</th>
<td></td>
<td>If <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> × <i>b</i> = 0</span>, then <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> = 0</span> or <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i> = 0</span> (or both)
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The first five properties listed above for addition say that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, under addition, is an <a href="/wiki/Abelian_group" title="Abelian group">abelian group</a>. It is also a <a href="/wiki/Cyclic_group" title="Cyclic group">cyclic group</a>, since every non-zero integer can be written as a finite sum <span class="nowrap">1 + 1 + ... + 1</span> or <span class="nowrap">(−1) + (−1) + ... + (−1)</span>. In fact, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> under addition is the <i>only</i> infinite cyclic group—in the sense that any infinite cyclic group is <a href="/wiki/Group_isomorphism" title="Group isomorphism">isomorphic</a> to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>.
</p><p>The first four properties listed above for multiplication say that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> under multiplication is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commutative_monoid" title="Commutative monoid">commutative monoid</a>. However, not every integer has a multiplicative inverse (as is the case of the number 2), which means that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> under multiplication is not a group.
</p><p>All the rules from the above property table (except for the last), when taken together, say that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> together with addition and multiplication is a <a href="/wiki/Commutative_ring" title="Commutative ring">commutative ring</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiplicative_identity" title="Multiplicative identity">unity</a>. It is the prototype of all objects of such <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_structure" title="Algebraic structure">algebraic structure</a>. Only those <a href="/wiki/Equality_(mathematics)" title="Equality (mathematics)">equalities</a> of <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_expression" title="Algebraic expression">expressions</a> are true in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/For_all" title="For all">for all</a> values of variables, which are true in any unital commutative ring. Certain non-zero integers map to <a href="/wiki/Additive_identity" title="Additive identity">zero</a> in certain rings.
</p><p>The lack of <a href="/wiki/Zero_divisor" title="Zero divisor">zero divisors</a> in the integers (last property in the table) means that the commutative ring <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is an <a href="/wiki/Integral_domain" title="Integral domain">integral domain</a>.
</p><p>The lack of multiplicative inverses, which is equivalent to the fact that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is not closed under division, means that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is <i>not</i> a <a href="/wiki/Field_(mathematics)" title="Field (mathematics)">field</a>. The smallest field containing the integers as a <a href="/wiki/Subring" title="Subring">subring</a> is the field of <a href="/wiki/Rational_number" title="Rational number">rational numbers</a>. The process of constructing the rationals from the integers can be mimicked to form the <a href="/wiki/Field_of_fractions" title="Field of fractions">field of fractions</a> of any integral domain. And back, starting from an <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_number_field" title="Algebraic number field">algebraic number field</a> (an extension of rational numbers), its <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_integers" title="Ring of integers">ring of integers</a> can be extracted, which includes <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> as its <a href="/wiki/Subring" title="Subring">subring</a>.
</p><p>Although ordinary division is not defined on <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, the division "with remainder" is defined on them. It is called <a href="/wiki/Euclidean_division" title="Euclidean division">Euclidean division</a>, and possesses the following important property: given two integers <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i></span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i></span> with <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i> ≠ 0</span>, there exist unique integers <span class="texhtml"><i>q</i></span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>r</i></span> such that <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> = <i>q</i> × <i>b</i> + <i>r</i></span> and <span class="texhtml">0 ≤ <i>r</i> &lt;  |<i>b</i>|</span>, where <span class="texhtml">|<i>b</i>|</span> denotes the <a href="/wiki/Absolute_value" title="Absolute value">absolute value</a> of <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i></span>. The integer <span class="texhtml"><i>q</i></span> is called the <i>quotient</i> and <span class="texhtml"><i>r</i></span> is called the <i><a href="/wiki/Remainder" title="Remainder">remainder</a></i> of the division of <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i></span> by <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i></span>. The <a href="/wiki/Euclidean_algorithm" title="Euclidean algorithm">Euclidean algorithm</a> for computing <a href="/wiki/Greatest_common_divisor" title="Greatest common divisor">greatest common divisors</a> works by a sequence of Euclidean divisions.
</p><p>The above says that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is a <a href="/wiki/Euclidean_domain" title="Euclidean domain">Euclidean domain</a>. This implies that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is a <a href="/wiki/Principal_ideal_domain" title="Principal ideal domain">principal ideal domain</a>, and any positive integer can be written as the products of <a href="/wiki/Prime_number" title="Prime number">primes</a> in an <a href="/wiki/Essentially_unique" title="Essentially unique">essentially unique</a> way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> This is the <a href="/wiki/Fundamental_theorem_of_arithmetic" title="Fundamental theorem of arithmetic">fundamental theorem of arithmetic</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Order-theoretic_properties">Order-theoretic properties</span></h2>
<p><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is a <a href="/wiki/Total_order" title="Total order">totally ordered set</a> without <a href="/wiki/Upper_and_lower_bounds" title="Upper and lower bounds">upper or lower bound</a>. The ordering of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is given by:
<span class="texhtml">:... −3 &lt; −2 &lt; −1 &lt; 0 &lt; 1 &lt; 2 &lt; 3 &lt; ...</span>
An integer is <i>positive</i> if it is greater than <a href="/wiki/0" title="0">zero</a>, and <i>negative</i> if it is less than zero. Zero is defined as neither negative nor positive.
</p><p>The ordering of integers is compatible with the algebraic operations in the following way:
</p>
<ol><li>if <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> &lt; <i>b</i></span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>c</i> &lt; <i>d</i></span>, then <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> + <i>c</i> &lt; <i>b</i> + <i>d</i></span></li>
<li>if <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i> &lt; <i>b</i></span> and <span class="texhtml">0 &lt; <i>c</i></span>, then <span class="texhtml"><i>ac</i> &lt; <i>bc</i></span>.</li></ol>
<p>Thus it follows that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbb {Z} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/449494a083e0a1fda2b61c62b2f09b6bee4633dc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.55ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> together with the above ordering is an <a href="/wiki/Ordered_ring" title="Ordered ring">ordered ring</a>.
</p><p>The integers are the only nontrivial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Totally_ordered" title="Totally ordered">totally ordered</a> <a href="/wiki/Abelian_group" title="Abelian group">abelian group</a> whose positive elements are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Well-ordered" title="Well-ordered">well-ordered</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> This is equivalent to the statement that any <a href="/wiki/Noetherian_ring" title="Noetherian ring">Noetherian</a> <a href="/wiki/Valuation_ring" title="Valuation ring">valuation ring</a> is either a <a href="/wiki/Field_(mathematics)" title="Field (mathematics)">field</a>—or a <a href="/wiki/Discrete_valuation_ring" title="Discrete valuation ring">discrete valuation ring</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_development">Traditional development</span></h3>
<p>In elementary school teaching, integers are often intuitively defined as the union of the (positive) natural numbers, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zero" title="Zero">zero</a>, and the negations of the natural numbers. This can be formalized as follows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> First construct the set of natural numbers according to the <a href="/wiki/Peano_axioms" title="Peano axioms">Peano axioms</a>, call this <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle P}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</math></span><img alt="P^{-}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/df5e7f2104dcc4156c6db49c5fe233e2f9e3fd91" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.332ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>, for example the ordered pair <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (0,0)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mn>0</mn>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (0,0)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="(0,0)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5d630d3e781a53b0a3559ae7e5b45f9479a3141a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:5.168ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>. Then the integers are defined to be the union <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle P\cup P^{-}\cup \{0\}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>∪<!-- ∪ --></mo>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>
<mn>0</mn>
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle P\cup P^{-}\cup \{0\}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/373648483c45baf3647c3bfb81f55a8fd22e11d7" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.73ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>. 
</p><p>The traditional arithmetic operations can then be defined on the integers in a <a href="/wiki/Piecewise" title="Piecewise">piecewise</a> fashion, for each of positive numbers, negative numbers, and zero. For example <a href="/wiki/Negation" title="Negation">negation</a> is defined as follows:

</p><p>The traditional style of definition leads to many different cases (each arithmetic operation needs to be defined on each combination of types of integer) and makes it tedious to prove that integers obey the various laws of arithmetic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Equivalence_classes_of_ordered_pairs">Equivalence classes of ordered pairs</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Relative_numbers_representation.svg"><img alt="Representation of equivalence classes for the numbers −5 to 5" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="494" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="318" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Relative_numbers_representation.svg/330px-Relative_numbers_representation.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Relative_numbers_representation.svg/495px-Relative_numbers_representation.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Relative_numbers_representation.svg/660px-Relative_numbers_representation.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Relative_numbers_representation.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Red points represent ordered pairs of <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">natural numbers</a>. Linked red points are equivalence classes representing the blue integers at the end of the line.</div></div></div>
<p>In modern set-theoretic mathematics, a more abstract construction<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> allowing one to define arithmetical operations without any case distinction is often used instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> The integers can thus be formally constructed as the <a href="/wiki/Equivalence_class" title="Equivalence class">equivalence classes</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ordered_pair" title="Ordered pair">ordered pairs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">natural numbers</a> <span class="texhtml">(<i>a</i>,<i>b</i>)</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell-1970-p83_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell-1970-p83-40">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>The intuition is that <span class="texhtml">(<i>a</i>,<i>b</i>)</span> stands for the result of subtracting <span class="texhtml"><i>b</i></span> from <span class="texhtml"><i>a</i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell-1970-p83_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell-1970-p83-40">[39]</a></sup> To confirm our expectation that <span class="nowrap">1 − 2</span> and <span class="nowrap">4 − 5</span> denote the same number, we define an <a href="/wiki/Equivalence_relation" title="Equivalence relation">equivalence relation</a> <span class="texhtml">~</span> on these pairs with the following rule:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (a,b)\sim (c,d)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>a</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>b</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>∼<!-- ∼ --></mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>c</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>d</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (a,b)\sim (c,d)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle (a,b)\sim (c,d)}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9eed2e08692e7ce42d13803af10157e550d6328" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.235ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>precisely when
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a+d=b+c.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>a</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>d</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>b</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>c</mi>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a+d=b+c.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle a+d=b+c.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/841eb6f725df18e7006fa0d5c4811b006236178c" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:13.876ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Addition and multiplication of integers can be defined in terms of the equivalent operations on the natural numbers;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell-1970-p83_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell-1970-p83-40">[39]</a></sup> by using <span class="texhtml">[(<i>a</i>,<i>b</i>)]</span> to denote the equivalence class having <span class="texhtml">(<i>a</i>,<i>b</i>)</span> as a member, one has:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle [(a,b)]+[(c,d)]:=[(a+c,b+d)].}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle -[(a,b)]:=[(b,a)].}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>The standard ordering on the integers is given by:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle [(a,b)]&lt;[(c,d)]}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle a+d&lt;b+c.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e67ade3d92d34e0bc68f6f59b0bad905d997c047" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:13.876ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>It is easily verified that these definitions are independent of the choice of representatives of the equivalence classes.
</p><p>Every equivalence class has a unique member that is of the form <span class="texhtml">(<i>n</i>,0)</span> or <span class="texhtml">(0,<i>n</i>)</span> (or both at once). The natural number <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> is identified with the class <span class="texhtml">[(<i>n</i>,0)]</span> (i.e., the natural numbers are <a href="/wiki/Embedding" title="Embedding">embedded</a> into the integers by map sending <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> to <span class="texhtml">[(<i>n</i>,0)]</span>), and the class <span class="texhtml">[(0,<i>n</i>)]</span> is denoted <span class="texhtml">−<i>n</i></span> (this covers all remaining classes, and gives the class <span class="texhtml">[(0,0)]</span> a second time since <span class="texhtml">−0 = 0.</span>
</p><p>Thus, <span class="texhtml">[(<i>a</i>,<i>b</i>)]</span> is denoted by
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{cases}a-b,&amp;{\mbox{if }}a\geq b\\-(b-a),&amp;{\mbox{if }}a&lt;b.\end{cases}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow>
<mo>{</mo>
<mtable columnalign="left left" columnspacing="1em" displaystyle="false" rowspacing=".2em">
<mtr>
<mtd>
<mi>a</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>b</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
</mtd>
<mtd>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
<mtext>if </mtext>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<mi>a</mi>
<mo>≥<!-- ≥ --></mo>
<mi>b</mi>
</mtd>
</mtr>
<mtr>
<mtd>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>b</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>

</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{cases}a-b,&amp;{\mbox{if }}a\geq b\\-(b-a),&amp;{\mbox{if }}a&lt;b.\end{cases}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\begin{cases}a-b,&amp;{\mbox{if }}a\geq b\\-(b-a),&amp;{\mbox{if }}a&lt;b.\end{cases}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b0c122ad0814aead2d6a7f4dd653dccd6315dd25" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:22.061ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>If the natural numbers are identified with the corresponding integers (using the embedding mentioned above), this convention creates no ambiguity.
</p><p>This notation recovers the familiar <a href="/wiki/Group_representation" title="Group representation">representation</a> of the integers as <span class="texhtml">{..., −2, −1, 0, 1, 2, ...} </span>.
</p><p>Some examples are:
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_approaches">Other approaches</span></h3>
<p>In theoretical computer science, other approaches for the construction of integers are used by <a href="/wiki/Automated_theorem_proving" title="Automated theorem proving">automated theorem provers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rewriting" title="Rewriting">term rewrite engines</a>.
Integers are represented as <a href="/wiki/Term_algebra" title="Term algebra">algebraic terms</a> built using a few basic operations (e.g.,  <b>zero</b>, <b>succ</b>, <b>pred</b>) and, possibly, using <a href="/wiki/Natural_number" title="Natural number">natural numbers</a>, which are assumed to be already constructed (using, say, the <a href="/wiki/Peano_axioms" title="Peano axioms">Peano approach</a>).
</p><p>There exist at least ten such constructions of signed integers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> These constructions differ in several ways: the number of basic operations used for the construction, the number (usually, between 0 and 2) and the types of arguments accepted by these operations; the presence or absence of natural numbers as arguments of some of these operations, and the fact that these operations are free constructors or not, i.e., that the same integer can be represented using only one or many algebraic terms.
</p><p>The technique for the construction of integers presented in the previous section corresponds to the particular case where there is a single basic operation <b>pair</b><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (x,y)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>y</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle (x,y)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="(x,y)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/41cf50e4a314ca8e2c30964baa8d26e5be7a9386" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:5.328ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> that takes as arguments two natural numbers <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle y}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>y</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="y" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b8a6208ec717213d4317e666f1ae872e00620a0d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.155ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span>, and returns an integer (equal to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x-y}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>y</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x-y}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x-y" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3129cb3620bd9f38d0304a0fca719644d7d2d265" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:5.326ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>). This operation is not free since the integer 0 can be written <b>pair</b>(0,0), or <b>pair</b>(1,1), or <b>pair</b>(2,2), etc. This technique of construction is used by the <a href="/wiki/Proof_assistant" title="Proof assistant">proof assistant</a> <a href="/wiki/Isabelle_(proof_assistant)" title="Isabelle (proof assistant)">Isabelle</a>; however, many other tools use alternative construction techniques, notable those based upon free constructors, which are simpler and can be implemented more efficiently in computers.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Computer_science">Computer science</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Integer_(computer_science)" title="Integer (computer science)">Integer (computer science)</a></div>
<p>An integer is often a primitive <a href="/wiki/Data_type" title="Data type">data type</a> in <a href="/wiki/Computer_language" title="Computer language">computer languages</a>. However, integer data types can only represent a <a href="/wiki/Subset" title="Subset">subset</a> of all integers, since practical computers are of finite capacity. Also, in the common <a href="/wiki/Two%27s_complement" title="Two's complement">two's complement</a> representation, the inherent definition of <a href="/wiki/Sign_(mathematics)" title="Sign (mathematics)">sign</a> distinguishes between "negative" and "non-negative" rather than "negative, positive, and 0". (It is, however, certainly possible for a computer to determine whether an integer value is truly positive.) Fixed length integer approximation data types (or subsets) are denoted <i>int</i> or Integer in several programming languages (such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algol68" title="Algol68">Algol68</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C_(computer_language)" title="C (computer language)">C</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/Object_Pascal" title="Object Pascal">Delphi</a>, etc.).
</p><p>Variable-length representations of integers, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bignum" title="Bignum">bignums</a>, can store any integer that fits in the computer's memory. Other integer data types are implemented with a fixed size, usually a number of bits which is a power of 2 (4, 8, 16, etc.) or a memorable number of decimal digits (e.g., 9 or 10).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cardinality">Cardinality</span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cardinality" title="Cardinality">cardinality</a> of the set of integers is equal to <span class="texhtml">ℵ<sub>0</sub></span> (<a href="/wiki/Aleph_number" title="Aleph number">aleph-null</a>). This is readily demonstrated by the construction of a <a href="/wiki/Bijection" title="Bijection">bijection</a>, that is, a function that is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Injective" title="Injective">injective</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surjective" title="Surjective">surjective</a> from <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="double-struck">Z</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {Z} }</annotation>
</semantics>

</p>

<p>with <a href="/wiki/Graph_of_a_function" title="Graph of a function">graph</a> (set of the pairs <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (x,f(x))}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<dl><dd><span class="texhtml">{... (−4,8), (−3,6), (−2,4), (−1,2), (0,0), (1,1), (2,3), (3,5), ...}</span>.</dd></dl>
<p>Its <a href="/wiki/Inverse_function" title="Inverse function">inverse function</a> is defined by
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{cases}g(2x)=-x\\g(2x-1)=x,\end{cases}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow>
<mo>{</mo>
<mtable columnalign="left left" columnspacing="1em" displaystyle="false" rowspacing=".2em">
<mtr>
<mtd>
<mi>g</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mn>2</mn>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>x</mi>
</mtd>
</mtr>
<mtr>
<mtd>
<mi>g</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mn>2</mn>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
</mtd>
</mtr>
</mtable>
<mo fence="true" stretchy="true" symmetric="true"></mo>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{cases}g(2x)=-x\\g(2x-1)=x,\end{cases}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\begin{cases}g(2x)=-x\\g(2x-1)=x,\end{cases}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9418caee54847103cc897959d0cd46c8fd074ba0" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:16.99ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>with graph
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="texhtml">{(0, 0), (1, 1), (2, −1), (3, 2), (4, −2), (5, −3), ...}</span>.</dd></dl>

<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">More precisely, each system is <a href="/wiki/Embedding" title="Embedding">embedded</a> in the next, isomorphically mapped to an subset.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The commonly-assumed set-theoretic containment may be obtained by constructing the reals, discarding any earlier constructions, and defining the other sets as subsets of the reals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Such a convention is "a matter of choice", yet not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div>

<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source" id="CITEREFEuler1771">Euler, Leonhard (1771). <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/1770LEULERVollstandigeAnleitungZurAlgebraVol1/page/n31/mode/2up" rel="nofollow"><i>Vollstandige Anleitung Zur Algebra</i></a> [<i>Complete Introduction to Algebra</i>] (in German). Vol. 1. p. 10. <q>Alle diese Zahlen, so wohl positive als negative, führen den bekannten Nahmen der gantzen Zahlen, welche also entweder größer oder kleiner sind als nichts. Man nennt dieselbe gantze Zahlen, um sie von den gebrochenen, und noch vielerley andern Zahlen, wovon unten gehandelt werden wird, zu unterscheiden.</q> [All these numbers, both positive and negative, are called whole numbers, which are either greater or lesser than nothing. We call them whole numbers, to distinguish them from fractions, and from several other kinds of numbers of which we shall hereafter speak.]</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Vollstandige+Anleitung+Zur+Algebra&amp;rft.pages=10&amp;rft.date=1771&amp;rft.aulast=Euler&amp;rft.aufirst=Leonhard&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2F1770LEULERVollstandigeAnleitungZurAlgebraVol1%2Fpage%2Fn31%2Fmode%2F2up&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AInteger"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source" id="CITEREFBourbaki1951">Bourbaki, Nicolas (1951). <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/algebrebour00bour/page/26/mode/2up" rel="nofollow"><i>Algèbre, Chapter 1</i></a> (in French) (2nd ed.).
